Output only the translation. <NL> English: were to be built in Italy. <NL> French:	 seraient construits en Italie <NL>  <NL> The French translation of "were to be built in Italy" is "seraient construits en Italie". This is because "were to be built" is a passive form that implies something will be constructed in the future under certain conditions or possibilities. In French, you would use the conditional tense of the verb "construire" (to build) which is "seraient construits" and add the preposition "en" followed by the country where it would be built, in this case, "Italy" or "l'Italie".
